  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bdc47dfb-8a36-4eff-8d82-106607bb99c1'

<span id="freeTextContainer5939900218495278170">Haunted by the loss of his mother and sister, Han Alister journeys south to begin his schooling at Mystwerk House in Oden’s Ford.   <span id="freeText5939900218495278170" style="display:none">Haunted by the loss of his mother and sister, Han Alister journeys south to begin his schooling at Mystwerk House in Oden’s Ford. But leaving the Fells doesn’t mean that danger isn't far behind. Han is hunted every step of the way by the Bayars, a powerful wizarding family set on reclaiming the amulet Han stole from them. And Mystwerk House has dangers of its own. There, Han meets Crow, a mysterious wizard who agrees to tutor Han in the darker parts of sorcery—but the bargain they make is one Han may regret. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Princess Raisa ana’Marianna runs from a forced marriage in the Fells, accompanied by her friend Amon and his triple of cadets. Now, the safest place for Raisa is Wein House, the military academy at Oden's Ford. If Raisa can pass as a regular student, Wein House will offer both sanctuary and the education Raisa needs to succeed as the next Gray Wolf queen. <br /><br />Everything changes when Han and Raisa’s paths cross, in this epic tale of uncertain friendships, cut-throat politics, and the irresistible power of attraction.</span>

    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1170312017?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1170312017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5153594945447662833"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Nobody's going to hand you anything. You don't get what you don't go after.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Well, I wanted a sequel as <b>mindblowing</b> as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_' title='The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Demon King</a> and I got it! I am under <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima' title='Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinda Williams Chima</a>'s spell!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468311314ra/19688813.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The pressure of past tragedies drove him forward - the need to escape reminders of his losses, and the desire to be somewhere other than where he'd been. <br/>That, and a smoldering desire for revenge.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>After losing everything he cared about, Han Alister is on his way to Oden's Ford to atten</span>
  <span id="freeText5153594945447662833" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Nobody's going to hand you anything. You don't get what you don't go after.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Well, I wanted a sequel as <b>mindblowing</b> as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_" title="The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a> and I got it! I am under <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima" title="Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinda Williams Chima</a>'s spell!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468311314ra/19688813.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The pressure of past tragedies drove him forward - the need to escape reminders of his losses, and the desire to be somewhere other than where he'd been. <br>That, and a smoldering desire for revenge.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>After losing everything he cared about, Han Alister is on his way to Oden's Ford to attend <b>
  <s>Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry</s>
</b> Mystwerk House, the academy for wizards, in order to become strong and fullfill his part of the deal with the clans. And exact revenge from the all-mighty Bayars. But Raisa is also heading to Oden's Ford, to attend the military academy and hide from her mother and the Wizard Council that wants to control her via a forced marriage and cause civil war in the queendom, while their enemies surround them. With only a couple of friends by their side, Han and Raisa have to study hard, practice even harder and make difficult decisions that may cost them everything they hold dear.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But it's not enough to know right from wrong. You need the strength to do what's right, even when what you want most in the world is the wrong thing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The first 100 pages were really slow, but the rest of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen__Seven_Realms___2_" title="The Exiled Queen (Seven Realms, #2) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exiled Queen</a> was an <b>absolutely enthralling tale of magic, politics and survival</b>! Of course I got a serious <b>Harry Potter vibe</b> but that's meant to happen every time I read about wizarding schools because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a> is the Queen! The insubordinate student with the great potential that always found trouble <i>(hello Harry Potter)</i>, the circle of elite students <i>(hello Professor Slughorn)</i>, the pull to dark magic <i>(Voldie? Is that you?)</i> and the annoying brat you can't help but picture like this<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468312736ra/19688978.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>there was a pattern that's for sure, but there was more. A strict military academy, travels to the realms of dreams, good manners tutoring, everything made up an intriguing story you couldn't stop reading! And the ever-present <b>politics</b> and <b>conspiracies</b> were enough to make you edgy and eager for answers! <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What's your heart saying now?”<br>“I'm in trouble.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>What prevented me for giving the fifth star even though I wanted to were the characters. There was Han, who survived the streets for being cunning, careful and methodical that all of the sudden started acting impulsively, recklessly and without thinking, endangering himself and his friends, while Raisa was reduced into a <b>hormone-driven silly teenager</b>. Her queendom was on the brink of war, but her constant concern was <i>who she'd kiss next and whether Amon loved her</i>. It was so <b>frustrating</b>, I wanted so badly to talk some sense into her thick skull!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468313844ra/19689164.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>She kept acting on a whim and making silly decisions like a petulant child instead of a future ruler (<i>the letter? Really?</i>), and I hated the way she treated Amon. She made a bad situation worse just because she couldn't have what she wanted. Raisa dear, just because Micah didn't kill you that doens't mean you should overlook everything he did, and you have to accept that your mother is a weak, bad queen. Denial will get you nowhere. And please, stop feeling dizzy and lightheaded every time someone kisses you! Your love life isn't more important than the fate of your world! <br><br><b>But if you overlook the wave of silliness that somehow hit the main characters, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen__Seven_Realms___2_" title="The Exiled Queen (Seven Realms, #2) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exiled Queen</a> was a wonderful magical adventure, and I can't wait to start the next installment!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467094006ra/19550484.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5153594945447662833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1613496345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1613496345" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1613496345?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1613496345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4681454185020088388"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝It's not enough to know right from wrong. You need the strength to do what's right, even when what you want most in the world is the wrong thing.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Rating: ★ ★ ★ ★ ½<br/><br/>HOLY CRAP. This book was literally everything. The Exiled Queen was such a major step up from The Demon King. This series just keeps getting better and better with each installment. I'm saying this straight out: <b>IF YOU HAVEN'T READ THE SEVEN REALMS SERIES, YOU BETTER GET A MOVE ON BECAUSE YOU ARE MISSING OUT.</b><br/><br/>The Exiled Que</span>
  <span id="freeText4681454185020088388" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝It's not enough to know right from wrong. You need the strength to do what's right, even when what you want most in the world is the wrong thing.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Rating: ★ ★ ★ ★ ½<br /><br />HOLY CRAP. This book was literally everything. The Exiled Queen was such a major step up from The Demon King. This series just keeps getting better and better with each installment. I'm saying this straight out: <b>IF YOU HAVEN'T READ THE SEVEN REALMS SERIES, YOU BETTER GET A MOVE ON BECAUSE YOU ARE MISSING OUT.</b><br /><br />The Exiled Queen was absolutely flawless. The characters, the plot, everything, had me hooked. The only negative thing I can say about this book or just the Seven Realms series in general is that it starts off really slow. But I'm beginning to think that this is just a trend in this series so I strongly recommend just being patient and getting through the first 150 pages or so because I guarantee that the rest of the book will BLOW YOUR MIND.<br /><br />Like most series in the literary world, each installment is an upgrade from the previous book, but it took me by surprise how much of an improvement The Exiled Queen was from The Demon King.<br /><br />We move away from politics and the Seven Realms as a whole and focus more on our younger characters as they all step foot on Oden's Ford to attend the academy. Our characters going off on their own to go to school was the cherry on top of a fantastic book. I got major HOGWARTS vibes while reading The Exiled Queen. I can't even stop saying how great this was.<br /><br />We got to see more of the characters finally interacting with one another, that being the Bayars and Han, and even Han and Raisa. We get more of Dancer and Cat! I liked Dancer in The Demon King but we never really got to see a lot of his character until The Exiled Queen. He was like the Ron Weasley of the Seven Realms. And I couldn't help but compare Micah Bayar to Draco Malfoy. Cat was also a pleasant addition to this installment. We definitely got to see her in action and although I was a bit wary of her at first, I took a liking to her towards the end. Fiona Bayar as well. Amon was probably the only one that I'm not sure I liked or not. I did before but not as much now. But I just loved seeing more of the characters rather than all the adults we had to deal with in the first book. It was definitely a breath of fresh air!<br /><br />Our two main characters Han and Raisa finally started interacting more but it was practically just a little tease! We got a taste of them as a couple and now I just have to have more. Cinda Williams Chima honestly takes slow burn romance to a whole new level. Our main characters are literally dancing circles around each other the whole book and only directly interact for a few chapters. But when they do... GAH. I'm constantly swooning and fanning myself.<br /><br />The Seven Realms has easily become one of my favorite series of all time and I still have two more books to go! I can't imagine how much better those next two will be. The Exiled Queen ended on such a high note and I'm just dying to start The Crimson Crown. More Han and Raisa please! &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="4681454185020088388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2384482748" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2384482748" />
    <a title="Tani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63414753-tani"><img alt="Tani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521292450p2/63414753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2384482748?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tani" href="/user/show/63414753-tani">Tani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2384482748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13180313731702860253"><b>RATINGS:  4 STARS </b><br/><br/><br/>The saga of the Seven Realms is continued by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen__Seven_Realms___2_' title='The Exiled Queen (Seven Realms, #2) by Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Exiled Queen</a> right from the point where its preceding book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_' title='The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Demon King</a> left off. The Exiled Queen shows more about character development than the previous book. This enchanted saga takes a step ahead to bring the readers an entanglement of different characters, a new perspective on the intentions of the characters and has introduced the venerable but neutral educational system of Oden’s Ford (is it only me who feels that it so</span>
  <span id="freeText13180313731702860253" style="display:none"><b>RATINGS:  4 STARS </b><br /><br /><br />The saga of the Seven Realms is continued by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen__Seven_Realms___2_" title="The Exiled Queen (Seven Realms, #2) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exiled Queen</a> right from the point where its preceding book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_" title="The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a> left off. The Exiled Queen shows more about character development than the previous book. This enchanted saga takes a step ahead to bring the readers an entanglement of different characters, a new perspective on the intentions of the characters and has introduced the venerable but neutral educational system of Oden’s Ford (is it only me who feels that it sounds similar to Oxford?) . Set in the backdrop of a war, the book has shown the repercussions and aftermath of such terrible and unpredictable times.<br /><br /><br />The book begins with Hanson Alister and Raisa ana’ Marianna travelling to Oden’s Ford, a boarding school, each carrying the weight of their past. So it's predictable that they're going to be in crossroads again. While Hans learns about the utilisation and power of his magic and the lifestyle of wizards and blue bloods, Raisa is focused on training herself to learn more about a life of a soldier to make herself a better queen in the future and being cautious at every turn to keep her identity a secret. Unlike in the preceding book, the protagonists learn to adapt themselves in the new surrounding, use their strengths to benefit themselves rather than showing it off with arrogance and learn to have different personality than the one they're habituated to. The resolution of the protagonists for retribution and bringing out welfare of the Fells has intensified. The secondary characters have made the story more ebullient and entrancing. The life in the boarding school was brought under spotlight to let us get more acquainted with the world of the Seven Realms. It was unique as it shows the combination of the academic patterns of the soldiers and the wizards. The world building and plot of the book was gripping and intriguing like it's previous book. The story is going to offer you an unexpected mixture of twists and turns which will compel you to grab the third book. The characters are layered with various shades and their roles in the book will leave you guessing and second guessing everything. There is a slow burn romance between the protagonists which is rare and unique in its own way but you're going to be disappointed again because they meet each other after the first half of the book. The chemistry between them is tested time and again which is quite similar to what happens in real life and it's quite rare to find the protagonists having different lives which doesn't involve having each other's constant presence.<br /><br /><br />Well, here comes my ranting. Honestly, I'm disappointed with the pace of the story. Like the first book, the book drags and drags and drags to the sea of boredom. The pace of the story in the first book was excusable but this time I don't think the suffering slow pace was necessary. Either the book should've kept up with the same pace as the pace with which the first book ended or the pace of the story should've been increased. Instead of that, we get the slow pace which frustrated and annoyed me like hell. There were too many unnecessary nitty-gritty details in the beginning. I wanted more of the relationship between Hans and Raisa.<br /><br /><br />Anyways, the book was more promising about the interesting things to come.<br /><br /><br />Thanks for reading my review. Happy Reading! 😊</span>
  <a data-text-id="13180313731702860253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1010899616" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1010899616" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010899616?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010899616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8045342754413823144"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457337486i/18346728._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let's be real, okay? <b>If I didn’t have to get up in 5 hours, I would dive in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409469.The_Gray_Wolf_Throne__Seven_Realms___3_' title='The Gray Wolf Throne (Seven Realms, #3) by Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Gray Wolf Throne</a> RIGHT NOW.</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“You couldn’t keep your mouth shut? I’m calling you Glitterhair from now on. Or Talksalot.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>I don’t know what is it with these books that keep me captivated and compelled to read more and more and more. <b>The characters' growth is fantastic, my boy Han fascinating, the plot way more surprising but it still contains several tropes that I usually don't like</b> - including an heroine who "loves"</span>
  <span id="freeText8045342754413823144" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457337486i/18346728._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's be real, okay? <b>If I didn’t have to get up in 5 hours, I would dive in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409469.The_Gray_Wolf_Throne__Seven_Realms___3_" title="The Gray Wolf Throne (Seven Realms, #3) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gray Wolf Throne</a> RIGHT NOW.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You couldn’t keep your mouth shut? I’m calling you Glitterhair from now on. Or Talksalot.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I don’t know what is it with these books that keep me captivated and compelled to read more and more and more. <b>The characters' growth is fantastic, my boy Han fascinating, the plot way more surprising but it still contains several tropes that I usually don't like</b> - including an heroine who "loves" several boys, BUT for once in a way that I can accept and understand, and without the constant change of mind that drives me nuts. Also, is this <i>really</i> love? She's confused and unsure, and that makes her more believable than ever. Raisa might be flawed, but she keeps going whatever happens and doesn't let heartbreak go in her way. The girl has <b>goals</b>, and boys aren't going to change them.<br><br><b><u>Don't be afraid, though</u> : the story does NOT focus on the romance at all, and the characters have responsibilities way more important than falling in love.</b> Think betrayals, clans, wizard's rivalries, old charms... What's not to love? <br><br>Moreover, the secondary characters are fleshed-out and their actions do have impact on the story - Dancer, Kat, Micah, Fiona, Amon - they all add something interesting and none of them is wasted. Also, HAN. Just give me a break, okay? The guy is wicked and adorable at the same time, how can I resist? Torn between his thirst for power and revenge and the deals he made, our Han Alister evolves into someone I loved to follow. But above everything else, I love that <b>none of the characters is either good or bad. GREY EVERYWHERE, I tell you.</b><br><br>The plot keeps thickening and promises a hell lot of action in the next two books, with all the threads linking together and the menace on all the characters' heads more and more present.<br><br>Anyway, off to bed I go, after these ramblings that may or may not be morphed into a real review tomorrow depending on my ability to restrain myself from reading book 3 (= closed to none). Oh hell. <b>I'm addicted</b>. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8045342754413823144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2061643108?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews">Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=fictional-war">fictional-war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=reviews-of-the-year">reviews-of-the-year</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=favorite-heroine">favorite-heroine</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2061643108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12278547908115111499">I honestly started this series with low expectations but the writing just captivated me with such visual characters that I felt like I was there with them. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600453708ra/30124198.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600279830ra/30115393.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Raisa is my fucking queen</b>, just slays everyone.<br/><br/> I love her so freaking much. Her character grows so much during this series, she becomes more confident yet kinda learns how to deal with her temper <i>*respect*</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“The wolves surrounded her, tongues lolling, ears flat, bumping their great heads against her middle, nearly knocking her over.<br/>“Great l</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText12278547908115111499" style="display:none">I honestly started this series with low expectations but the writing just captivated me with such visual characters that I felt like I was there with them. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600453708ra/30124198.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600279830ra/30115393.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Raisa is my fucking queen</b>, just slays everyone.<br><br> I love her so freaking much. Her character grows so much during this series, she becomes more confident yet kinda learns how to deal with her temper <i>*respect*</i><br><br><b>
  <i>“The wolves surrounded her, tongues lolling, ears flat, bumping their great heads against her middle, nearly knocking her over.<br>“Great lot of good you do me,” she grumbled. “Why can’t I teach you to attack wizards on command?”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605654105ra/30391483.gif" width="170" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Raisa's sass made me laugh so hard at times. She is so practical <i>yet</i> a dreamer. A warrior <i>yet</i> learns to manipulate in politics with the best of them. And she makes mistakes. So so so many mistakes. But she keeps trying and keeps sassing the shit out of everything-including magical beings. <br><br>Now can we give a little shoutout for the group dynamics! I love adore reading about friendships-- Han and Dancer are a brilliant example of how to build such an iconic duo of complex characters that support each other<br><br><b>
  <i>“Dancer’s blue eyes glinted with amusement. “Now say, ‘Copperheads are little more than leeches on the body of society—a necessary evil.’”<br>Han laughed. “I don’t think I can manage. Guess I’m not cut out for this.”</i>
</b><br><br>They continued to be hilarious troublemakers together, figuring out how to live as wizards and studying <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605654105ra/30391484.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book also incorporates legit training *thank gawd* and the characters don't unrealistically master their abilities overnight. <br><br><i>
  <b>“The library’s closed, Alister. I thought everybody had already gone.”<br>“Sorry,” Han said. “I fell asleep.” He paused by the desk. “What day is it?”<br>The proficient grinned. “You need to quit working so much. It’s Sunday.”</b>
</i><br><br>I HATE it when books go <u>poof now you all-powerful, congrats kid.</u><br><br>But the best part part this book is that <b>FINALLY</b> Raisa AND Hans plot lines TWINE TOGETHER <br><br><b>AND FUCK YES I SHIP THEM, I SHIP THEM SO HARD I MIGHT BREAK THE GODDAMN BOAT</b> <br><br>Guys this is the <b>slow-burn developing relationship&lt;---</b>and that shit is so rare it practically on the endangered trope list <br><br>And then there's this scene. This fucking scene that broke my heart. Han learns how much he loves Raisa <b> via her secret identity</b> and he just reflects over their times together. <br><br><b>
  <i>“She was prickly and proud, used to ordering people around and getting her own way. She was smart and opinionated—she could talk the tail off a dog. But she was fiercely kindhearted—she’d cross the street to give a coin to a beggar, and always backed the underdog in any fight. She’d shed tears over Mam and Mari—though she’d never even met them.<br>She demanded a lot—but demanded even more from herself.”</i>
</b><br><br>And then our ending. Will Raisa ever see Han again and if so could they build a relationship after so many lies? <br><br><b><i>“And what did she expect to build on that shaky foundation? By the way, Alister, I’ve been lying to you for more than a year; I’m actually a member of the royal family you despise. There’s no future for us, but I’d still like to be friends.”</i><br><br>Well fuck I hope so. Next book please!!</b></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311180195" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311180195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8324950198263962344"><b>Re-read 2016</b><br/> <br/>If you you were on the fence about the first book, I'm <i>begging</i> you to give #2 a chance!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458225449ra/18459082.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is where <i>everything</i> starts to come together & make sense in a big way.<br/>In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124518754' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Demon King</a>, Han & Rasia's lives only intersect for a small portion of the book. I believe the main reason for that is because the author wanted each of them to have full backstories, including other romantic interests. I <i>love</i> that <b>both</b> of these characters have been in love before, and that their boyfriends/girlfriend</span>
  <span id="freeText8324950198263962344" style="display:none"><b>Re-read 2016</b><br> <br>If you you were on the fence about the first book, I'm <i>begging</i> you to give #2 a chance!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458225449ra/18459082.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is where <i>everything</i> starts to come together &amp; make sense in a big way.<br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124518754" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a>, Han &amp; Rasia's lives only intersect for a small portion of the book. I believe the main reason for that is because the author wanted each of them to have full backstories, including other romantic interests. I <i>love</i> that <b>both</b> of these characters have been in love before, and that their boyfriends/girlfriends weren't horrible people. It adds a touch of realism to the storytelling...in my opinion.<br>But in <i>this</i>, Han &amp; Rasia's lives intertwine a bit more at Oden's Ford, and (bonus!) there are some huge spoilery <b>REVEALS</b> that happen in this one!<br>I'm probably botching this review, but (again, in MY opinion) <b>The Exiled Queen</b> is where shit really starts to get good.<br>Read it! <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458226131ra/18459155.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Original Review: 2012</b><br>I didn't want to finish this book, but I mean that in a good way. I just didn't want to have to stop reading!<br><br>I thought the plot was great, even though I'm not normally so in love with how Fantasy is written. I usually find it a tad bit boring when it comes to the world-building in this genre, and I'll admit it...the weird names usually throw me for a loop. However, the way the lives of the main characters in this story were interwoven into each other was so interesting, that I couldn't help but enjoy reading every last bit of this book. <br><i>It also possibly helped that I could (I think) pronounce all of the names</i>.<br><br>One more thing I want to mention, and then I'm going to go...<br><i>I've got <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409469.The_Gray_Wolf_Throne__Seven_Realms___3_" title="The Gray Wolf Throne (Seven Realms, #3) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gray Wolf Throne</a> in my hot little hands right now, and I can't wait to start reading it!</i><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In the first book and the beginning of this one, several of the characters seemed to have found true love, or at least the beginnings of it. Toward the end of this one, you learn that for some of them, it isn't going to be possible for them to be together (for whatever reason). The interesting thing about this series, is that even though they were heartbroken, they were also all <i>moving on</i>. You know, <i>getting over it</i>. No one was suicidal or anything. Such a <i>strange</i> concept to find in YA. <br>I think I'm a little in love with Chima for that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8324950198263962344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138721159" class="readable"
              >

So there were some aspects that I sort of enjoyed MORE I guess.. <span id="freeTextContainer6562340996574000405">Yay! I love fantasy again!!!<br/><br/>Yet, I still hate reviewing fantasy - with an added emphasis on the word hate. <br/><br/>Most books = Point A to point b. <br/><br/>Fantasy books = Point A intersects with person C on the way to meeting person F at point Y. <br/><br/>How the heck do you review that?<br/><br/>I'll reiterate what I've loved about <i>Seven Realms</i> so far. These books meet the criteria for what I'd like to see more of in YA fantasy. There is action and adventure. There are plenty of varied characters from all walks of life. There i</span>
  <span id="freeText6562340996574000405" style="display:none">Yay! I love fantasy again!!!<br /><br />Yet, I still hate reviewing fantasy - with an added emphasis on the word hate. <br /><br />Most books = Point A to point b. <br /><br />Fantasy books = Point A intersects with person C on the way to meeting person F at point Y. <br /><br />How the heck do you review that?<br /><br />I'll reiterate what I've loved about <i>Seven Realms</i> so far. These books meet the criteria for what I'd like to see more of in YA fantasy. There is action and adventure. There are plenty of varied characters from all walks of life. There is an element of romance without it choking out the rest of the story. The books will appeal to a broad base of readers, even lovers of adult fantasy. Nothing here feels dumbed down or excessively youthful. In fact, I'd say these books are more mature than a good portion of the adult crap I've read lately. No joke. <br /><br />Whether you're new to fantasy or it's an old love, I'd say this series is worth checking out. It has a little bit of something for everyone.<br /><br />I might add more later, but maybe not. Fantasy still owns my ability to review, apparently. </span>

<div id="review_1428777285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428777285" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1428777285?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1428777285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6736751410385557200">ALL THE LOVE TO THIS INCREDIBLY UNDERRATED SERIES. All. the. love, I tell you. Excuse me, but I think I fell in love with 2 or 29 characters. <b>I just feel so monstrously HAPPY after reading such an epic book!!!</b> Not that it's a <i>happy</i> book. hahahaa. No. NO it's not. But it's amazingly written and the characters are adorable and the development is extraordinary and I'M JUST SO INVOLVED. <b>It's the kind of book that absolutely <i>swallows</i> you while you read.</b><br/><br/>WHERE EVEN TO START? OMG. <br/><br/>Okay but let's talk ab</span>
  <span id="freeText6736751410385557200" style="display:none">ALL THE LOVE TO THIS INCREDIBLY UNDERRATED SERIES. All. the. love, I tell you. Excuse me, but I think I fell in love with 2 or 29 characters. <b>I just feel so monstrously HAPPY after reading such an epic book!!!</b> Not that it's a <i>happy</i> book. hahahaa. No. NO it's not. But it's amazingly written and the characters are adorable and the development is extraordinary and I'M JUST SO INVOLVED. <b>It's the kind of book that absolutely <i>swallows</i> you while you read.</b><br /><br />WHERE EVEN TO START? OMG. <br /><br />Okay but let's talk about characters. <b>Because this is definitely a majorly character-driven story.</b> We still have 2 points-of-view -- Princess Raisa and Han Alister. But there are a whole swam of secondary characters who are epic. AND SO DIVERSE. &lt;3 Be still me thumping heart. I adore diversity, okay?!<br /><br /><b>• Hans:</b> OMG I LOVE HANS. He's sassy and snarky and tough and yet he's got a marshmallow buttery inside with so much feeeeeeeelings. And he's still so rough around the edges. AND ALSO A WIZARD NOW. Watching him learn how to magic was wonderful. And he has so many sassy comebacks. Basically, one of my favourite protagonists of ever. <br /><b>• Raisa:</b> Ahhhh I LOVE HER TOO. This is seriously a series where BOTH narrations intrigued me 100%. I didn't even pick a favourite. I mean, maaaybe I like Hans a bit more? But Raisa is tough and smart and intelligent. Plus she's short and has a darkish complexion/hair so I totally look a bit like Raisa AND THEREFORE I AM QUEEN. BOW. *ahem* That aside, I like how Raisa is more emotionally venerable in this book, but she definitely NEVER collapses into a puddle. And I love how she totally smashes faces of annoying people. Go Raisa!<br /><b>• Amon:</b> Ehhhh. Okay, I like Amon. I do. But I think he's an idiot. He's gotten into his whole "duty is my god" complex and it's frustrating. He's made it clear he CAN'T be in love with Raisa, but he totally is. Ergo he gets a bit of an ownership thing over her, at the same time as disgarding her, and basically it made me dislike him. But he's an excellently written character.<br />•<b>Cat:</b> Tbh, I don't really love her. She's cool and sassy and she's like a street rat who'll jump sides as convienent. But she wasn't IN the story enough. <br />•<b>Dancer:</b> Speaking of characters not in the story enough...DANCER MY DARLING, WHY ARE YOU BARELY AROUND?!?!? He is like the book's biggest weakness, I think!! I love Dancer, but he's seriously only ever there if it's convenient to Han. Han does acknowledge he's not paying enough attention to his friends. BUt Dancer has the "I am just a secondary character with no real need to plot right now" thing going on. No other characters suffer from this!! So I don't get it why he is!!<br /><b>• Micah:</b> Is it just me or is he basically Draco Malfoy? HAHAHA. AHEM. I liked Micah more in the first book. He seemed more in a "grey area" but now he seems like he's just gonna be evil.<br /><b>• Fiona:</b> Micah's sister!! I didn't even know she existed in the first book (but maybe I missed it?) either way ME LIKEEE. She seems tough and snarky and with the potential for evil or greatness. Probably both. <br /><b>• Crow:</b> He's like this creepy guy in the dream world who is teaching Hans to be an epic wizard. BUT HE'S PROBABLY EVIL. I hope we get answers as to who he is eventually. <br /><br />...so basically the characters are A+ in excellent and just afjdkalsd I get so many feeeeeels towards them.<br /><br />Speaking of <i>feels</i>, <b>omg the romance was THE BEST THING EVER.</b> Yes it potentially strays into love-triangle territory...but at the same time it's not?? ANYWAY. RAISA + HANS = MY SHIP FOREVER. They don't even meet until pg 400!! But when they're together....afjdkslafjdlkaj they're so adorable and the quips are perfect and they're awkward and gorgeous and cute around each other and hiding their feelings and ZOMG KISS YOU LITTLE ADORABLE TWERPS.<br /><br />Least to say, I ship it. One of my favourite ships of ever.<br /><br />I'm sure it will sink and I will be destroyed in later books. I JUST HAVE THIS FEELING.<br /><br /><b>This one mostly takes place at the academies too.</b> So basically there is a wizard academy and then next door there is an army academy. SO IT'S AWESOME. Raisa ends up in Weir house (the army side) and Hans is at Mystwerk (the wizard side). And I looooved the wizards stuff!! It reminded me of Hogwarts, but in a completely DIFFERENT way (so don't fret about copying). I wish it'd been a little more detailed? But at the same time I loved what was there.<br /><br /><b> My only niggling doubts come at the ending.</b> I didn't think it was as smooth as the rest of the book? And also very rushed. There are so many plot twists and changes of direction in the last 60 pages that...woah. It was really hard to take it all in. I don't think Raisa put up enough of a fight. Same as Hans. Like they're both such hUGELY strong characters...but the seemed to be so easily pounded into the terrors at the end of the book. <br /><br />Yes. I said TERRORS AT THE END OF THE BOOK. <br /><br />Omg, please someone save my life and give me the next book asap before I LITERALLY EXPLODE FROM MY EYEBROWS. I JUST...wow. <b>I love this series, it's rapidly becoming one of my favourites of ever</b>. There were so many times when I shrieked and hugged the book (although my copy is darn heavy and I nearly killed myself once with it) and I just can't flail enough. EVERYONE NEEEEEEDS THIS SERIES IN THEIR LIFE OKAY? OKAY.<br /><br />Okay I'll go calm down now. <br /><br />(afjdklafjsdlk i totally will not)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6736751410385557200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1905494756" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17044338463446575272"><b>
  <i>"Nobody's going to hand you anything. You don't get what you don't go after.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I really enjoyed The Demon King so I went in with pretty high hopes for this book and I was not disappointed at all. This book was great - even better than <i>The Demon King</i>. I seriously wish that these books didn't have such a slow start! Although, I definitely think that the way this book left off, we (hopefully) should be getting a faster start since everything is going to shit. Okay, so basically it was slow for ab</span>
  <span id="freeText17044338463446575272" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Nobody's going to hand you anything. You don't get what you don't go after.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I really enjoyed The Demon King so I went in with pretty high hopes for this book and I was not disappointed at all. This book was great - even better than <i>The Demon King</i>. I seriously wish that these books didn't have such a slow start! Although, I definitely think that the way this book left off, we (hopefully) should be getting a faster start since everything is going to shit. Okay, so basically it was slow for about 100-200 pages of this since our characters were all travelling to our weird school thing where you can be basically any career ever. <br /><br />I'd definitely say that Han's chapters were more interesting this time around. I did enjoy his chapters in <i>The Demon King</i> but he was just far more interesting in his new situation. Raisa is just as good as ever and I honestly just love her. Her page time was definitely cut shorter though since Han had <b>a lot</b> of stuff to go through and learn.<br /><br />Let me tell you that there's so many feels and potential ships in this book. Every sort of interaction between any characters had me thinking: DO I SHIP IT?! Let's just say it right now: <b>I ship Han and Raisa</b> a lot. This is my end game couple and I will go down with this ship. Their relationship grew so much and I need <b>so many more chapters of this pair interacting.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Rai," Amon said, taking her hands in his. "Whatever you do, don't fall in love with him."<br />Raisa nodded, knowing it was already too late.</i>
</b><br /><br />Some other feels: Micah is a very confusing character. I'm torn between wanted to keep an open mind on him but sometimes I just want to punch him in the face. I feel like he has such potential and he would make a great ally if he would stop listening to his stupid father. I'm hoping he has some great character development! Also, Fiona could have some good character development if she wasn't so EVERYTHING IS MINE AND I AM ENTITLED TO EVERYTHING. I just want the Bayar's to fix their shit and be good allies. Amon is a character I'm high key waiting to die. Hear me out, I like him and I don't want him to die BUT he's such a killable character. He's Raisa's guard and I would run out of fingers if I tried to list every guard that died in a book. I'll actually be shocked if he survives all of the book. <br /><br />GIMME THE NEXT BOOK ASAP AND EVERYONE SHOULD READ THESE BOOKS</span>
  <a data-text-id="17044338463446575272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/606196367?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=o-captain-my-captain">o-captain-my-captain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer606196367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12962730605311061066"><b>Re-reading for the release of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23253083.Flamecaster__Shattered_Realms___1_' title='Flamecaster (Shattered Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flamecaster</a> with some peeps at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br/><br/><b>Original Review</b><br/><br/>Definitely for Fantasy Lovers of all ages.<br/><br/>Han and Raisa are both now headed separately to Oden’s Ford for training. Han needs to learn how to harness the power inside him to be able to fulfill the deal he made with the clans. Raisa needs to hide from her mother and a forced marriage she didn’t want until it is safer to come home. There seems to be danger around every corner for both of them.<br/><br/>Raisa</span>
  <span id="freeText12962730605311061066" style="display:none"><b>Re-reading for the release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23253083.Flamecaster__Shattered_Realms___1_" title="Flamecaster (Shattered Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">Flamecaster</a> with some peeps at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br /><br /><b>Original Review</b><br /><br />Definitely for Fantasy Lovers of all ages.<br /><br />Han and Raisa are both now headed separately to Oden’s Ford for training. Han needs to learn how to harness the power inside him to be able to fulfill the deal he made with the clans. Raisa needs to hide from her mother and a forced marriage she didn’t want until it is safer to come home. There seems to be danger around every corner for both of them.<br /><br />Raisa is traveling under the guise of Rebecca Morley with Amon Byrne and his triple. She has hopes of learning how to be a warrior queen like Hanalea. With the help of Amon she is learning how to fight and the feelings between them blossom but he made a deal with his father and Honor Duty and the magical bond seem to be getting in the way. <br /><br />Han made a promise to the clans in exchange for the money for his training at Odens Ford but it is a dangerous place with Micah Bayer around. It seems everyone wants to use Han in some way for their own ends. But he finds an unlikely mentor named Crow in the dream world. Han is busy trying to learn as much as possible and stay alive with all the ‘accidents’ happening around him. Han runs into Rebecca and they form a friendship. Han needs to learn how to be a blueblood and Rebecca agrees to teach him.<br /><br />This book has so much description in it. The fantasy world is completely built up and there is a real feel for the characters development. No one seems to be all good or all bad they all make good and bad decisions. There were some very heartbreaking moments and others you wanted to cheer for. Han is a very likeable scoundrel and never seems to forget his roots. Raisa is learning how to be a better Queen. While living with real people she gets sense for kingdom and yearns to do better than her Mother.<br /><br />This is a great second book in the seven realms series, definitely better than the first book as all of the character develop and really grow. There is a little bit of everything for fantasy lovers. Sure there are so plot devices that maybe didn’t need to be there but I liked the book so much I ignored them. Be ready to want to dive into the next book right after finishing.<br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694842129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8161697969701888168"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381112532ra/4243180.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I'm actually writing this as I come to and end of the third book. Why, you ask? Because despite my blatant dislike for the first book, and my not so impressed mood of the second book, I do believe this is a series worth trying. It actually reminds me of a couple of series, that while I despised the first book, the latter ones came to grow on me until I couldn't help but fall in love. Hopefully, that is the case here.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420405616ra/13219122.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>While they seem to have no clear plot or drive, as you read, you see many tibits</span>
  <span id="freeText8161697969701888168" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381112532ra/4243180.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I'm actually writing this as I come to and end of the third book. Why, you ask? Because despite my blatant dislike for the first book, and my not so impressed mood of the second book, I do believe this is a series worth trying. It actually reminds me of a couple of series, that while I despised the first book, the latter ones came to grow on me until I couldn't help but fall in love. Hopefully, that is the case here.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420405616ra/13219122.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>While they seem to have no clear plot or drive, as you read, you see many tibits that will ultimately come together, or at least I'm assuming, to make a worthwhile story. Now yes, this review is definitely being influenced by the third book, but the fact that I dove straight into the third book without even pausing to write a review for this one holds bearing of its own. <br><br>The characters are growing into likable people you can root for. The line of loyalty is being blurred and one thing I have come to love is the grayness of it all. No one is wholly good or completely bad, they're a mix of both and that in it of itself, is something rarely found in YA literature. New characters come into play, new alliances are forged, betrayals come to light. The plot, and I do say this loosely, is thickening and I, for one, and excited as heck to see the outcome. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423848897ra/13682089.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522268507?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexie" href="/user/show/20726801-lexie">Lexie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7861761823905474215">No, really. This book is the lovechild of Harry Potter and The Name of the Wind, with an extra pump of sass and hilarity, except it's set in a queendom, and everyone's some version of a half-blood mutt. It's basically all my favorite things in one.</span>

<div id="review_1170496420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1170496420" />
    <a title="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38570248-taylor-of-elfhame"><img alt="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603671693p2/38570248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1170496420?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" href="/user/show/38570248-taylor-of-elfhame">Taylor of Elfhame ❦</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1170496420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17483779115908646987">I want to say first off that I enjoyed this book so much more than book one. And really, I can’t explain why, but I’m going to try. With book one I felt like nothing was really going on almost, but now it feels more like it was just the first puzzle piece and couldn’t be fully appreciated without seeing the rest of it. I feel as though I’m in the middle of the story, and then the book is bam over and I have to run and fetch the next one to keep going. It’s not like cliffhangers, really, because </span>
  <span id="freeText17483779115908646987" style="display:none">I want to say first off that I enjoyed this book so much more than book one. And really, I can’t explain why, but I’m going to try. With book one I felt like nothing was really going on almost, but now it feels more like it was just the first puzzle piece and couldn’t be fully appreciated without seeing the rest of it. I feel as though I’m in the middle of the story, and then the book is bam over and I have to run and fetch the next one to keep going. It’s not like cliffhangers, really, because that implies a certain level of resolution. This series genuinely just feels like one long book split into four parts. And maybe that sounds bad, but it really isn’t. I like it a lot actually, I’m just not used to it. That’s the best explanation I give. But what is so lovable about this series is absolutely it’s characters. <br />Before I get into that though I want to ask someone who has read these books, if anyone has, to hear out my question and answer in the comments if you would. The question contains <b>spoilers</b> obviously, as does the rest of the review so if you’ve yet to read them you’ve been warned. <br />It was revealed at the end of book one that Han was descended from the Demon King, and apparently so was Raisa. And that’s cool and everything, but I ship them pretty hardcore (I’m not sure I’m supposed to I can’t really help it but nevermind that). Raisa has even expressly stated more than once that she loves him. Is the shared-ancestors thing an issue?? Because the Breaking was a thousand years ago, there’s got to have been at least 40 generations separating them (especially with how young they marry in the Seven Realms). I’m not sure if they can even be classified as related anymore. I don’t know, someone please tell me if this ever even comes up or if I’m just biting my nails over nothing. <br /><br />Now, anyways: Han. Oh my love. In book one I loved him, but in this book he came into himself so well. I’m so proud of how gifted he is. I love his charm and his sass. I am just sort of really annoyed that he still doesn’t know who Raisa really is at this point. When he was delivering his whole speech to her about blaming the Crown and she just sat there and took it I could not believe. I’m sick of him being ignorant about this, I just really want him to find out. That’s all I ask at this point. <br />And Raisa. Baby girl gives her heart away entirely too easily. I felt awful for her about what happened with Amon. I mean, I want her to be with Han so I wasn’t like pissed or anything but the guy you love taking some vows and then literally being in pain and sick to his stomach if he gives into any desire for you at all. That’s just rough. And Raisa is a sweetheart she didn’t deserve that. I hope that she doesn’t get her heart broken again with Han, that would break <i>my</i> heart. Raisa is also a badass though. The scenes where that creep tried to rape her and she took him down.<br /><br /><i>“You touch me again, you arrogant Ardenine swine, and I swear on the blood of Hanalea the warrior, I will</i> geld <i>you. Do you understand?”<br />Tourant nodded violently, sweat beading on his forehead.</i> <br /><br />Or when that assassin came to kill her and she took him out. I was just so proud of her. She can be elegant and proper one second and savage the next if need be. I adore her character. One thing, though. Something is going on with that ring she’s got, and I’m ridiculously curious. When she tried to take it off at the end there and it wouldn’t budge, red flags galore. I expect answers.<br /><br />The Bayars are such a pain in the ass. We know the High Wizard is a sociopath. But both his children are just psychos. Fiona was less annoying just because she wasn’t trying to kill Han every five seconds, but Micah was just intolerable. Like, give it a rest. And then kidnapping Raisa so she’ll be forced to marry him. Just. Wow. Micah’s just a problem that needs to be <i>hushed</i> in my opinion. <br />And speaking of problems: Crow was the shadiest of the shady from minute one. I have sooo many theories about this guy that I couldn’t even voice them all. Every time Han would meet with him I would get so anxious. Everything about him said <i>not to be trusted</i> and lo and behold. <br /><br />Amon is just a sympathy case. Dancer getting with Cat was welcome but predictable, I liked it alright. Hallie and the rest of Raisa’s friends were great I loved their banter and such. I don’t have much else to say, I’m looking forward to book three. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17483779115908646987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_110339828" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110339828" />
    <a title="Samantha Franks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3875410-samantha-franks"><img alt="Samantha Franks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510598479p2/3875410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110339828?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha Franks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha Franks" href="/user/show/3875410-samantha-franks">Samantha Franks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110339828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6385131416259293179">I like Cinda Wiliams Chima. Her previous books had her on my 'will watch with eagle eye' list. But the Seven Realm novels have landed her smack dab in the middle of my 'need to cyber stalk write like her' list.<br/>See, I like huge fantasy books, but I do agree, some of them can get dull. I didn't have that problem with this one. Instead of focusing on ornate descriptions and oodles and bunches of fantastical creatures, The Exiled Queen is full of characters that I love. While the plot is great and t</span>
  <span id="freeText6385131416259293179" style="display:none">I like Cinda Wiliams Chima. Her previous books had her on my 'will watch with eagle eye' list. But the Seven Realm novels have landed her smack dab in the middle of my 'need to cyber stalk write like her' list.<br />See, I like huge fantasy books, but I do agree, some of them can get dull. I didn't have that problem with this one. Instead of focusing on ornate descriptions and oodles and bunches of fantastical creatures, The Exiled Queen is full of characters that I love. While the plot is great and the writing is superb, it was the characters that really made this novel. <br />Raisa, the princess, is not the typical fluff ball. However, she isn't the now-typical 'I am a warrior princess' either. She's brave and flawed and stubborn and smart. Oh, and she really has this issue with kissing boys she shouldn't be kissing. <br />And speaking of that . . .<br />Let's just talk about Han, the main male character. Because, generally, fantasy novels do have great guys. But they aren't always crush worthy.<br />Yeah . . .<br />Han is. A reformed thief who can cheat at cards or slit a throat, Han is now becoming a magician. And through the whole book, even when I wasn't busy thinking Why are there no reformed thief-now-magician boys in my high school? I just liked him. <br />The villians are believable. And the support characters are just as fleshed out as the main ones. You want to be the friend of Dancer, Han's closest comrade, and you laugh as Raisa's roommates try and set her up.<br />Sequels are not always so hot. But honestly, I liked The Exiled Queen more than the previous novel. (Oddly, a pattern that seems to be repeating itself -- I liked Linger more than Shiver, Catching Fire more than Hunger Games, and now The Exiled Queen more than The Demon King.)<br />Still, the first is definitely good. I'm not saying that it isn't. I'm just saying that I think the second falls more into the 'Fantabulous' category. Cinda Williams Chima took on a subject that many people totally couldn't. It would have been easy for this to fall flat, or to bore me, but it didn't. I was too busy falling in love with the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6385131416259293179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2387925850" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2387925850" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=read-with-my-kids">read-with-my-kids</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387925850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13027997553916290302">Another great audiobook with my kids! I think I agree with all the other reviewers who say they like this second book even better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_' title='The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Demon King</a>.<br/><br/>The worldbuilding continues in layers and, since we got such a good foundation in the first book, the richness of it really shines through here. I love that Chima continues to deliver very thorough independent stories for both Han and Dancer and for Raisa and Amon. This means that by the time Han and Raisa actually meet up (quite a ways into this b</span>
  <span id="freeText13027997553916290302" style="display:none">Another great audiobook with my kids! I think I agree with all the other reviewers who say they like this second book even better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_" title="The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a>.<br /><br />The worldbuilding continues in layers and, since we got such a good foundation in the first book, the richness of it really shines through here. I love that Chima continues to deliver very thorough independent stories for both Han and Dancer and for Raisa and Amon. This means that by the time Han and Raisa actually meet up (quite a ways into this book) they each feel like fully realised and independently strong characters.<br /><br />My kids certainly enjoyed this as much or more than the first book. Normally we listen to audiobooks while driving in the car but towards the end of this, they were both wanting to listen to it at home just to see how it was going to end. Needless to say, we started book 3, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409469.The_Gray_Wolf_Throne__Seven_Realms___3_" title="The Gray Wolf Throne (Seven Realms, #3) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gray Wolf Throne</a>, immediately on finishing this one.<br /><br />This is a great series so far, with a lot of depth and an interesting story and characters. It's perfect for both younger audiences as well as those who enjoy YA fantasy, and an excellent choice to read or listen to together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13027997553916290302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2486033289126486484"><b>*** 4.25 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the fantastic Fantasy lovers at BB&B!</b><br/><br/>Started with the travel of all our young characters, be it good or bad, unknowingly ending up in the same town, same school and at the same time - talk about a coincidence:-)<br/><br/>Once at the school, our 4 main characters, Han, Raisa, Amon and Dancer all have to deal with the typical for being the new kid at school issues on top of the never ending blows their respective faiths have dealt them by the virtue of their births... The const</span>
  <span id="freeText2486033289126486484" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.25 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the fantastic Fantasy lovers at BB&amp;B!</b><br /><br />Started with the travel of all our young characters, be it good or bad, unknowingly ending up in the same town, same school and at the same time - talk about a coincidence:-)<br /><br />Once at the school, our 4 main characters, Han, Raisa, Amon and Dancer all have to deal with the typical for being the new kid at school issues on top of the never ending blows their respective faiths have dealt them by the virtue of their births... The constant game of hide and seek would have been funny had it not been for the life and death steaks. Treacherous allies and ruthless enemies are everywhere and trust is a rare commodity. Can true friendships survive the assault and could new love bloom among half truths and expectations of betrayal??? Well, read it people, I am not telling!!! <br /><br />This book was written beautifully and the plot thickens with every passing chapter... The characters are growing under the difficult circumstances and the best and worst are coming into the light... And if you are a Fantasy lover of the ages between 1 and 111 years old I promise you to enjoy it!!! <br /><br />On a separate note, the Head Wizard and Mac Gillan <b>HAVE TO DIE!!! </b><br /><br />I am anxious to get to the next book and wish all of you Happy Reading!!!</span>
