<div id="review_164512244" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164512244" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164512244?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=point-of-view-girl">point-of-view-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=all-kinds-of-fantasy">all-kinds-of-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=annoying-characters">annoying-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=just-the-worst">just-the-worst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=not-my-type">not-my-type</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=point-of-view-guy">point-of-view-guy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164512244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9664537981406105889">Ahh, what can I say about this series? It's like George Martin fantasy for younger audiences (only that's not exactly fair to George Martin - at least the guy knows how to create dynamic, intriguing characters. Chima's <i>Seven Realms</i> series, by contrast, is populated solely by wet noodles). <b>Boo</b>. I don't recommend this series, and I won't be continuing with it. <br/><br/><b>Longer review of the overall series</b><br/>Here's the thing...this series really frustrates me. This is the kind of series that screams 'READ ME AM</span>
  <span id="freeText9664537981406105889" style="display:none">Ahh, what can I say about this series? It's like George Martin fantasy for younger audiences (only that's not exactly fair to George Martin - at least the guy knows how to create dynamic, intriguing characters. Chima's <i>Seven Realms</i> series, by contrast, is populated solely by wet noodles). <b>Boo</b>. I don't recommend this series, and I won't be continuing with it. <br /><br /><b>Longer review of the overall series</b><br />Here's the thing...this series really frustrates me. This is the kind of series that screams 'READ ME AMELIA! You're going to LOVE ME!' Because, see...I lovelovelove high fantasy, probably more so than any other genre/subgenres. Most books that deal with magical and/or fantastical elements are set in the modern world, so true high fantasy novels get my attention faster than cake with icing and the smell of popcorn.<br />Plus...look at those covers. LOOK AT THEM.<br />So all these things said, I really wanted to like these books. I wanted so much to enjoy them, love them, and recommend them. But...I didn't. And I most certainly do NOT recommend this series, whatsoever.<br /><br />Plot wise, there were some things that I think could have been done differently. But what really killed this series, for me, were the characters. The two "protagonists," Han and Raisa, were yet more examples of characters that I felt obligated to care about, but really disliked.<br />Raisa is yet another of those heroines who thinks the world revolves around her and whose sense of self-preservation borders on extreme, and Han...just don't get me started on that loser. The supporting characters didn't leave much of an impression, and I really wish that three characters in particular - Amon, Micah, and Bird - would have been axed entirely. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[pretty much any of the dopey love interests. I mean, this reads like a fantasy version of "Days of Our Lives." Bleh <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />More than any other genre, it seems like fantasies are the most removed from reality and the reaches of real-world restrictions. They are the most magical, and traditionally, the most epic. And I guess what really disappoints me is the lack of 'epic-ness' with this series. Plus...there's another quality that traditional fantasy characters have possessed that sadly seems to be rapidly diminishing: true heroes. <br />In the past, fantasy characters were noble. They were <i>virtuous</i>. Yeah okay, maybe a little innocent, but still...they were inspiring, and they represented innocence, integrity and goodness. No, Frodo Baggins was not 'street-smart.' He wasn't snarky, smooth-talking, or edgy. Neither were any of the hobbits, really, unless you consider Pippin and Merry's ability to persuade Treebeard to fight against Saruman "smooth-talking." One of the greatest young adult fantasy series of all time is the <i>Chronicles of Prydain</i>, and its protagonist, Taran the Assistant Pig-Keeper, didn't have any of those personality traits, either. I guess what disappoints me is how cliched the "sassy angry chick" and "smooth-talking bad boy" characters have become, even in high fantasy. The tone of the <i>Seven Realms</i> books, one of the few true high fantasies of current YA lit, is just so different from traditional fantasies and so similar to the majority of other YA books out there. It's attempting to be edgy and subversive, because edgy and subversive is COOL, donchano? Except...not. Also, in my original review I mentioned feeling like the target audience is a bit off. The design and marketing skews young, but the series reads like fantasy "Degrassi" <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay, I readily admit that "Degrassi" was a guilty pleasure indulgence when I was in high school, but come on. Wouldn't you feel just a little bit squeamish about 11-year olds watching it? And honestly...the show's not that good. Stupid characters and tired cliches placed on an assembly line of contrived storylines. Just like this series. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />To be fair, nothing I've mentioned here is exclusive to <i>Seven Realms</i> alone. Quite a few YA books I've read recently have had one or several of these elements, too. So while I love the explosion of YA literature in the last 10-15 years, and while I am glad that "kids today" have more options than when I was a kid/middle-schooler, I wish that they could experience the kind of high fantasy characters I grew up reading and loving.<br /><br />In my opinion, Chima's <i>Seven Realms</i> series is the YA equivalent of George R.R. Martin's books ("edgy fantasy."), and therefore, they are not books that I would recommend - either to my friends, students, or family members. After all, a book's cover doesn't tell the whole story...<br />Please let me say again that this is just my opinion, and just my thoughts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9664537981406105889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1351774501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1351774501" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1351774501?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423121374" href="/book/show/9640847-the-exiled-queen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1351774501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12386577395169639300"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>I loved this book better than the first! I'm hoping they all keep getting better! <br/><br/>All of the characters both good and bad end up at the same school! They are all set up in different houses. You have wizards, learning to fight, book work, etc. <br/><br/>And Raisa who was such a little twit in the beginning of the first book, has redeemed herself even more in this book. I still believe she will make a great Queen. I feel sorry for her and Amon. She has known him all of he</span>
  <span id="freeText12386577395169639300" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br><br>I loved this book better than the first! I'm hoping they all keep getting better! <br><br>All of the characters both good and bad end up at the same school! They are all set up in different houses. You have wizards, learning to fight, book work, etc. <br><br>And Raisa who was such a little twit in the beginning of the first book, has redeemed herself even more in this book. I still believe she will make a great Queen. I feel sorry for her and Amon. She has known him all of her life and wants to be with him but since he's a part of the Queen's guard he is below her status. This means nothing to Raisa and she wants to make it work no matter what anyone says, but there is a little hiccup in that situation. I won't give out the spoiler. It's just sad, but that's the way it goes. <br><br>Raisa runs into Han at school and starts tutoring him. I'm hoping maybe something will happen with these two as they can be all powerful together and destroy the jerks in the book! <br><br>Raisa is actually going by the name Rebecca Morley so no one will recognize her as the princess, as she ran away from home. Her mother, the queen, has been enthralled by her Captain of the Guard and lets just say that's a whole other crock of.... <br><br>Han has no idea she is the queen. He met her as Rebecca back in their home land. Some really horrible stuff has happened to Han and I really hope this doesn't turn him evil, it is a huge possibility due to his heritage. Now, don't get me wrong, he can kill off all the jerks in the book and that is fine. I just don't want him going down the ole<b> He Who Shall Not Be Named road!</b> Han is in the same building as Dancer and they work together on learning their spells etc. <br><br>There are some cool new characters in the book and some that I'm not too sure about yet. <br><br>And there is stupid Micah and his crew in the school trying to cause trouble for Han as usual. He does something kinda nice at the end, but you can't trust him. He's probably putting up some kind of front. <br><br>I love this series so far and I hope it continues that way. I think anyone that likes young adult fantasy, sword and sorcery type stuff would like this book series as well. You be the judge of that :) <br><br><a href="http://s1379.photobucket.com/user/melmartD11/media/book%20banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437402575i/15581842._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo book banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12386577395169639300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16040667542497005880" style="display:none">Well THAT was a whirlwind of crazy emotions... and I freaking loved it.<br /><br />So ok. The first half of this book is completely dragging... slow, but still somehow rich and somewhat interesting... but I was definitely wondering when all our characters were gonna be thrust back together. (Also uhm... hello Harry Potter world.) Whatever. I still adore this world. Slow building or not, it is completely fascinating and so well put together. <br /><br />Holy crap of the world... the second half of the book. Er ok.. maybe more like the last third... I can't remember... because once it hits.. you're done for. I feel like I still have whiplash or something. <br /><br />I don't even know how to handle the rest of my feels so this is all I got..<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Amon. </u>
</b>Good freaking heavens can I please hug you. My heart just breaks for you WHY ARE YOU SO PERFECTLY SWEET and UGH. FEELS. FEELS. FEELS. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Nope, I will never get over him or what he did for Raisa or how freaking heart breaking his story is.   <u>Raisa</u>
</b>. Congrats. You've made it to my all time favorite heroines list. (Can we just appreciate for a moment that she's badass- but not unbelievable? Like she's the perfect blend of young/naive but strong willed and completely determined and unswayable. She's not going down without a FIGHT.)<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Han.</u>
</b> Why the frolic are you the sweetest thing under the sun? Like how can I not love this boy? Ugh. Like I even need to say this but um...Adorbs. Cuteness overload. FEELS. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and those scenes with Raisa? YAS. YAS YAS.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Micah.</u>
</b> Whatever you know I'm destined to find you intriguing. Sorry not sorry that I really like you.<br /><br />But seriously guys- this series is a blast. I absolutely recommend this to anyone looking for a hella-fun and crazy wild journey. <br /><br />Yeah ok. <div id="review_1806952134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1806952134" />
    <a title="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy"><img alt="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480352284p2/33795465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1806952134?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" href="/user/show/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy">Nouf *LostinFantasy*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=books-with-maps">books-with-maps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=forbidden-love-angst">forbidden-love-angst</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806952134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9234995410358170856"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But it’s not enough to know right from wrong. You need the strength to do what’s right, even when what you want most in the world is the wrong thing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>4 stars! (Would give it 3.5 to be objective but my enjoyment level pushes it up).<br/><br/>I'm having <b>such a great time</b> reading this series!<br/><br/>The setting is different from the first book -- the characters go to neighboring wizard and military schools! I really enjoyed the school setting. And for a while in the book, the characters in the wizard sc</span>
  <span id="freeText9234995410358170856" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But it’s not enough to know right from wrong. You need the strength to do what’s right, even when what you want most in the world is the wrong thing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />4 stars! (Would give it 3.5 to be objective but my enjoyment level pushes it up).<br /><br />I'm having <b>such a great time</b> reading this series!<br /><br />The setting is different from the first book -- the characters go to neighboring wizard and military schools! I really enjoyed the school setting. And for a while in the book, the characters in the wizard school (Han, Dancer, Micah, Fiona...) have no idea that the princess is in disguise and enrolled as a cadet across the bridge with Amon and his crew.<br /><br />And I'm not usually a fan of school settings -- it's part of why I'm not a fan of contemporary YA -- but here, it's more like <b>a year long training and preparing for the dangers and war building back in their home.</b><br /><br />The web of intrigue and political conflict keeps twisting further in the queendom despite our MC's being away from the conflict and in school. But there's <b>lots of plotting and secrets</b> surrounding them and reaching them. (I still need to know who Crow -- Han's mysterious tutor -- is!).<br /><br /><b>The book starts a bit slow</b> (a chunk is spent with them being on the road on their way to the school), but then <b>picks up the pace and I couldn't put it down!</b><br /><br /><b>I enjoyed the character development</b> the most in this book! <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Just because you’re the enemy of my enemy don’t mean you’re my friend, Han thought.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />In the first book, I couldn't get a feel for <b>Han</b>'s "streetlord" side very much. And near the end, his feelings after everything was taken from him didn't get much focus. <b>But in this book, it's all over him</b> -- his anger and hate towards his enemies, his drive for revenge, and his daring attitude. And he's in the same school with his enemies and "blueblood" wizards he never thought he'd have to measure up against. More than that, <b>despite every powerful person trying to use him for their own agendas, he's kind of using them for his own interests and plans too.</b> I'm excited to see how that works out in the next books (I expect lots of trouble for him)! <br /><br /><b>Raisa</b> really could become one of my favorite female MC's! <br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>I tend to stir people up, not settle them down.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />She has more reason to doubt herself, she's in disguise, she's out of her element but works hard to learn and adapt. But outside of her refuge, she's still in the focus of every twisted and dangerous plot. In the previous book, she's wondered if it's just the dress and jewelry that make her a princess but now, she has none of that but <b>retains that strength of character that shows the queen she'll be.</b> Except when she's trying to navigate her love life...<br /><br />To be honest, <b>I wasn't as annoyed by the love triangle</b> as I might have been. It helps that I like both the guy characters -- Han is great of course, and Amon is a perfect cutie pie that I adore so much!! But she doesn't fall for them at the same time and I think the feelings and heartbreak she goes through teach her something about herself that <b>just adds to her character growth.</b><br /><br />Raisa and Han's interactions (and romance) are also interesting because <b>he still thinks she's Rebecca Morley, former upperclass tutor, and not the Princess heir</b> -- who he's already grouped with all the people responsible for the terrible things he went through.<br /><br />And did I just mention how much I love <b>Amon</b>? Because I do! It's a shame he didn't get even one POV chapter in this book, but he's still a prominent character. I know that the <b>"good", loyal, and steadfast characters</b> aren't people's favorite but I tend to like them as much as the morally dubious ones. Especially when <b>they're tortured but take it in stride like Amon.</b><br /><br />Another wonderful character is <b>Dancer</b> -- who I wish had a bigger role than just Han's loyal BFF. But I loved the addition of <b>Cat</b> as their friend too, and I actually shipped Cat and Dancer the second they met even though she's so awful to him! <br /><br />As for <b>Micah</b>, he spent most of the book being a rip off of Draco Malfoy, and I was disappointed because he showed a lot of potential as a gray and morally confused character in the previous book. But near the end of the book that potential creeped back up (only in scenes with Raisa, apparently), so I'm back to being a bit interested in what his future choices will be.<br /><br />There's a lot more characters in this book and <b>you don't know who to trust, and who could be a future threat or ally!</b> It's fun!<br /><br />But the series is <b>still tropey</b> so far (there's some Harry Potter/Hogwarts deja vu here and there), <b>but I don't mind that.</b> It's still such an engaging read and overall <b>the story keeps building and is keeping me hooked!</b><br /><br />I've already started the following installment! <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9234995410358170856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2374880258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18149518296566001211">I'm not a fan of journeys. Why couldn't we just start at the school?<br/><br/>No real villain in this one. Micah was more bully than baddie and Fiona was sorta likeable. Crow could be a villain, but I don't think he's evil. (That's not to say I'd trust him.)<br/><br/>I love magic schools! But although the book was still good, the school and the magic were disappointing. We got one magic lesson, ONE! In the whole book! <br/><br/>Also, very few new characters were added, considering there's a whole school full of new people. W</span>
  <span id="freeText18149518296566001211" style="display:none">I'm not a fan of journeys. Why couldn't we just start at the school?<br /><br />No real villain in this one. Micah was more bully than baddie and Fiona was sorta likeable. Crow could be a villain, but I don't think he's evil. (That's not to say I'd trust him.)<br /><br />I love magic schools! But although the book was still good, the school and the magic were disappointing. We got one magic lesson, ONE! In the whole book! <br /><br />Also, very few new characters were added, considering there's a whole school full of new people. We meet one annoying student girl, but that's about it outside of Micah's friends. Han also only seemed to have one teacher, (that we saw or heard about) asside from the dean. They're both good characters, don't get me wrong, but <b>a magic school book this is not. </b><br /><br />Since we also had to spend time with Raisa. She was much nicer this book, less princess-like and selfish. But she'll never be my favorite character. I loved that she has friends now. Though it was disappointing how little time she spends with Amon. <br /><br />It took more than half the book for our main characters to meet up again. Their getting to know each other was more bicker than banter but their new relationship wasn't all bad. I do wish they'd just be friends. I know, I need to get past that because obviously they're going to be a couple. Ugh. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Even if they are kind of distantly related. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Things get exciting at the end, just in time for a cliffhanger!</span>

<div id="review_2758860548" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2758860548" />
    <a title="AbigailHaleigh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39161421-abigailhaleigh"><img alt="AbigailHaleigh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485702307p2/39161421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2758860548?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AbigailHaleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AbigailHaleigh" href="/user/show/39161421-abigailhaleigh">AbigailHaleigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2758860548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8084302863165843613">I will definitely be talking about this book more on my channel. But so far, I am very pleasantly surprised by this series. Considering it's one of the "older ya series" I was worried about how the diversity and world building would be, but it's been fantastic. I always think that there can be more lgbtq+ characters, but there is a mention of a lesbian couple, and a mention of an entire group of women loving women, and honestly...where do I sign up?<br/><br/>The plot of this book is a bit more drawn out I</span>
  <span id="freeText8084302863165843613" style="display:none">I will definitely be talking about this book more on my channel. But so far, I am very pleasantly surprised by this series. Considering it's one of the "older ya series" I was worried about how the diversity and world building would be, but it's been fantastic. I always think that there can be more lgbtq+ characters, but there is a mention of a lesbian couple, and a mention of an entire group of women loving women, and honestly...where do I sign up?<br /><br />The plot of this book is a bit more drawn out I think than the first one, but I'm such a sucker for a school plot, so I loved learning about the different areas of the school. The wizarding side vs. the more military side. Overall, I'm just finding this series very entertaining and easy reads to get through, and I'm excited to start the third book! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8084302863165843613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2215384029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2215384029" />
    <a title="nicklein" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6058998-nicklein"><img alt="nicklein" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552791879p2/6058998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2215384029?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nicklein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nicklein" href="/user/show/6058998-nicklein">nicklein</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2215384029&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2215384029" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15049780674545784722">This would be a very upsetting book if <b>(a)</b> Raisa didn’t escape, <b>(b)</b> Han didn’t plan to take the road which leads directly to Raisa and <b>(c)</b> I didn’t like the synopsis of The Gray Wolf Throne so much.<br/><br/>The first chapter was the best recap ever because my memory has failed me yet again. As much as I hate Gillen and wish him to be gutted, I liked reading from his perspective. I kinda remembered what went down with TDK, which was good because I was reading chapter 1 too slow for my liking.<br/><br/>The next coup</span>
  <span id="freeText15049780674545784722" style="display:none">This would be a very upsetting book if <b>(a)</b> Raisa didn’t escape, <b>(b)</b> Han didn’t plan to take the road which leads directly to Raisa and <b>(c)</b> I didn’t like the synopsis of The Gray Wolf Throne so much.<br /><br />The first chapter was the best recap ever because my memory has failed me yet again. As much as I hate Gillen and wish him to be gutted, I liked reading from his perspective. I kinda remembered what went down with TDK, which was good because I was reading chapter 1 too slow for my liking.<br /><br />The next couple of chapters flew by because I had one goal in mind: to get to the reunion of Han and Raisa before sleeping. And...with that (stupid)mindset, I almost finished the book. Yay me. Not because they reunited near the end but because it was so good. I was intrigued by everything — mainly everything that’s happening in the Mystwerk House.<br /><br />I’m not a big fan of Raisa here, to be completely honest. I hate how she claimed to be pining for Amon but also acted totally in love with Han a minute later.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Whatever you do, don’t fall in love with him.”<br />Raisa nodded, knowing it was already too late.</b>
</i><br /><br />Me iz confused. <br /><br />I still ship her with Han so bad though. So. So. Bad. You don’t know how many times I wished for them to hook up whenever they meet. The wait nearly killed me. It was worth it though.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I live in the present,” Han said, “because the future is always chancy. When it comes to being with you, I’m willing to take the risk. Are you?”</b>
</i><br /><br />Hanson Allister — what a great name for someone so dumb at times. I’m so glad luck’s on his side because he did a lot of stupid things in this book. Goading Fiona at the west gate? Accepting drinks from a stranger? Picking a fight at Micah not even hours before getting to Oden? Trusting Crow? The list goes on. I was getting tired of it but it’s part of his charm I think.<br /><br />Han is still my favorite character in this series though, despite his recklessness and arrogance.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Grief was like that. It gradually faded into a dull ache, until some simple sight or sound or scent hit him like a hammer blow.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I loathe the Bayars.<br /><br />I hate how I didn’t feel Dancer’s presence here.<br /><br />I hate how every character seems to be in love with the main characs. My eyes nearly stuck at the back of my head from rolling them too much.<br /><br />Amon reminded me so much of Chaol. It was driving me nuts. I want to ship him and Raisa but I had a feeling it’s doomed from the start since TDK that’s why I refuse to ship them no matter what. I’d be mad to ship them, they’re a ticking time bomb of heartbreak. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“But it’s not enough to know right from wrong. You need the strength to do what’s right, even when what you want most in the world is the wrong thing.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Still refusing.<br /><br />Anyway, how could you be so naive to think that you’re in love with someone but be giddy at the thought of another person’s touch and still remember how that person touched you when he took you hostage before? Yes, I’m looking at you, Raisa.<br /><br />This book has drained me as if I’ve been at Aediion for a week. That’s the truth.<br /><br />My head is aching so bad right now for lack of sleep. I’ve been reading nonstop for at least 8 hours, took a quick doze and picked up the book again to finish the last hundred pages. It was exhausting and I. Loved. Every. Minute. Of. It. <br /><br />I can’t sleep without knowing how it would end. <br /><br />Afterward, I reached for the third book immediately because I can’t live for the next 12 hours without reading the synopsis of TGWT.<br /><br />Book, what have you done to me?<br /><br />I’m scared to pick up TGWT even though the synopsis satisfied me. I don’t know why. I think I need assurance. <br /><br />I need to know whether Han and Raisa will get married (aaaaaaaaaaaaa they betta) and rule Seven Realms together.<br /><br />But at the same time I’m terrified to find out they don’t and I end up ditching the series. This only proved that I only live for my ship. Ughhhhhhhh I hate myself.<br /><br />I’m still on the fence if I’m going to pick up TGWT right away. Welp, wish me luck and read this series at your own risk. It’s really, really, really great but it also has the potential to drive you crazy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15049780674545784722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HRZRKdl27vbmEJCirc9koIEsv689hVVmL/qUUdf6kJeaLmfKBrsWBr2bDi+tJCNf8F5AuCk03wMcA4xh+RznxQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bALq5EvFFyu7MX7Aw2spye0P/0Tyu84h3fq7rh78C27rOtwHlAjv2+C64E3DgG42nH0AU+YKRETuA6OeMBp8PA==')})
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12048644804913164145">New York Times bestselling author Cinda Williams Chima comes from a long line of fortune-tellers, musicians and spinners of tales. She began writing romance novels in middle school, which were often confiscated by her teachers.<br/><br/>Her Heir Chronicles series (magic comes to contemporary Ohio) comprises <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213647.The_Warrior_Heir' title='The Warrior Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Warrior Heir</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/500743.The_Wizard_Heir' title='The Wizard Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wizard Heir</a> . <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2866413.The_Dragon_Heir' title='The Dragon Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dragon Heir</a> The Enchanter Heir, and the Sorcerer Heir. <br/><br/>Chima's</span>
  <span id="freeText12048644804913164145" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author Cinda Williams Chima comes from a long line of fortune-tellers, musicians and spinners of tales. She began writing romance novels in middle school, which were often confiscated by her teachers.<br /><br />Her Heir Chronicles series (magic comes to contemporary Ohio) comprises <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213647.The_Warrior_Heir" title="The Warrior Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior Heir</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/500743.The_Wizard_Heir" title="The Wizard Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wizard Heir</a> . <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2866413.The_Dragon_Heir" title="The Dragon Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Heir</a> The Enchanter Heir, and the Sorcerer Heir. <br /><br />Chima's Seven Realms series launched with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King" title="The Demon King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a> in 2009; I<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen" title="The Exiled Queen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exiled Queen</a> in 2010. The Gray Wolf Throne in 2011, and The Crimson Crown (2012.).<br /><br />Her Shattered Realms quartet comprises Flamecaster ( 2016) Shadowcaster (2017) Stormcaster (2018) and Deathcaster scheduled for March 5, 2019. <br /><br />Chima is a graduate of Case Western Reserve University and the University of Akron. Chima has been a workshop leader, panelist, and speaker at writing conferences, including the Northern Ohio SCBWI Conference, the Western Reserve Writers’ Conference, and the World Fantasy Convention. She frequently speaks to young writers and readers at schools and libraries nationwide. <br /><br />Chima lives in Ohio with her family, and is always working on her next novel. </span>

She aspires to be like Hanalea—the legendary warrior queen who killed the Demon King and saved the world.
